This looks like a Pell-type equation. Pell equations usually have the form x² - Dy² = N. Here, D is 4 and N is -3. The general Pell equation form is x² - Dy² = N. Here, D=4, N=-3. Pell equations with D a perfect square are different because the continued fraction expansion of sqrt(D) is finite, so Pell equations with D a square have only a finite number of solutions. Wait, D=4 is a square, so maybe this equation has only a finite number of solutions.In general, when D is a perfect square, say D = k², then the equation x² - k² y² = N can be written as (x - ky)(x + ky) = N. So, in our case, (a - 2b)(a + 2b) = -3.Since a and b are positive integers, and a - 2b and a + 2b are integers. Also, since a and b are positive, a + 2b is positive. 🔑:(x, y)=(0,0) is obviously a solution. Furthermore, the equation can be written as: (2 y+1)^{2}= 4 y(y+1)+1=x^{2}+x+1, for x>0, x^{2}+x+1, strictly between x^{2} and (x+1)^{2}, cannot be a perfect square.

❓:Among the following functions, the odd function is (    )A: y=x^{2}sin xB: y=x^{2}cos xC: y=|ln x|D: y=2^{-x}

🧠:[<think>Okay, so I need to figure out which of these functions is odd. Let me recall what an odd function is. An odd function satisfies the condition f(-x) = -f(x) for all x in its domain. That means if I plug in -x into the function, it should be the same as taking the negative of the original function. Got it. Let's check each option one by one.Starting with option A: y = x² sin x. Let's test if this is odd. Compute f(-x). Replace x with -x: (-x)² sin(-x). Simplify that. (-x) squared is x², right? Because (-x)*(-x) = x². Then sin(-x) is -sin x because sine is an odd function. So f(-x) = x²*(-sin x) = -x² sin x. Compare that to -f(x). The original function f(x) is x² sin x, so -f(x) = -x² sin x. So f(-x) = -f(x). That means option A is an odd function. Hmm, that seems to satisfy the condition. Wait, but maybe I should check the other options too to be sure.Option B: y = x² cos x. Let's do the same. Compute f(-x) = (-x)² cos(-x). (-x) squared is x² again. Cosine is an even function, so cos(-x) = cos x. Therefore, f(-x) = x² cos x. Compare to -f(x). The original function f(x) is x² cos x, so -f(x) = -x² cos x. Therefore, f(-x) = x² cos x ≠ -f(x) unless x² cos x is zero. But in general, it's not equal. So option B is even, not odd.Option C: y = |ln x|. Hmm, the absolute value of the natural logarithm. Let's check the domain first. The natural logarithm ln x is defined for x > 0. So the domain here is x > 0. But an odd function must be defined for x and -x. Since the domain is only positive numbers, we can't even check f(-x) because it's not defined for negative x. Therefore, this function isn't odd because it doesn't satisfy the symmetry required for odd functions. So option C is out.Option D: y = 2^{-x}. Let's check. Compute f(-x) = 2^{-(-x)} = 2^{x}. Compare to -f(x) = -2^{-x}. So f(-x) = 2^{x}, which is not equal to -2^{-x} unless for specific x. For example, at x = 1: f(-1) = 2^{1} = 2, and -f(1) = -2^{-1} = -0.5. Clearly not equal. So D is not odd.So, going back, only option A satisfied f(-x) = -f(x). Let me double-check with a specific value. Let's take x = π/2. Then for A: f(π/2) = (π/2)^2 sin(π/2) = (π²/4)*1 = π²/4. C isn't defined for negative x, so can't be odd. D is an exponential function, which is neither even nor odd. So for negative x, the function isn't even defined. Therefore, we can't really talk about f(-x) because it's not in the domain. So since the function isn't defined for negative x, it can't be odd (or even), because odd and even functions need to satisfy the condition for all x in their domain, which would have to be symmetric around 0. The answer is A.Final Answerboxed{A}</think>To determine which function is odd, we need to check if ( f(-x) = -f(x) ) for all ( x ) in the domain of the function.Option A: ( y = x^2 sin x )- Compute ( f(-x) ): [ f(-x) = (-x)^2 sin(-x) = x^2 (-sin x) = -x^2 sin x = -f(x) ]- This satisfies the condition for an odd function.Option B: ( y = x^2 cos x )- Compute ( f(-x) ): [ f(-x) = (-x)^2 cos(-x) = x^2 cos x = f(x) ]- This is an even function, not odd.Option C: ( y = |ln x| )- The domain of ( ln x ) is ( x > 0 ), so ( f(-x) ) is not defined for negative ( x ). Therefore, it cannot be odd.Option D: ( y = 2^{-x} )- Compute ( f(-x) ): [ f(-x) = 2^{-(-x)} = 2^x ]- Compare with ( -f(x) ): [ -f(x) = -2^{-x} ]- Since ( 2^x neq -2^{-x} ) for all ( x ), this is not an odd function.Thus, the odd function is (boxed{A}).]

🔑:To determine which function is an odd function, we recall that a function f(x) is odd if and only if f(-x) = -f(x) for all x in the domain of f.- For option A, y=x^{2}sin x, we have f(-x) = (-x)^{2}sin(-x) = x^{2}(-sin x) = -x^{2}sin x = -f(x). Therefore, option A is an odd function.- For option B, y=x^{2}cos x, checking f(-x) = (-x)^{2}cos(-x) = x^{2}cos x = f(x), which does not satisfy the condition for an odd function.- For option C, y=|ln x|, this function is not defined for x leq 0, so it cannot be an odd function.- For option D, y=2^{-x}, checking f(-x) = 2^{x}, which does not satisfy f(-x) = -f(x).Thus, the odd function among the given options is boxed{text{A}}.

🔑:68. Let's take a point K on BC (Fig. 14) such that widehat{K A C}=60^{circ}, M K | A C. The Hamming distance between two codewords is the number of positions in which they differ. For subsets, this corresponds to the size of the symmetric difference. The symmetric difference of two subsets A and B is |AΔB|=|A| + |B| - 2|A∩B|=5 +5 -2|A∩B|=10 -2|A∩B|. Therefore, the Hamming distance is 10 -2|A∩B|. Therefore, requiring |A∩B| ≤2 is equivalent to requiring the Hamming distance ≥10 -4=6. Therefore, a binary code with constant weight 5, length 10, and minimal Hamming distance 6 corresponds to our problem. According to coding theory, the maximum number of such codewords is 18. Understanding the Constraints: - Each subset ( A_i ) has exactly 5 elements. - The intersection of any two subsets ( A_i ) and ( A_j ) has at most 2 elements.2. Key Inequalities: - The total number of element occurrences across all subsets is ( 5k ). - The average number of subsets each element is in is ( frac{5k}{10} = frac{k}{2} ).3. Double Counting Argument: - The total number of pairs of subsets is ( binom{k}{2} ). - Each pair of subsets can share at most 2 elements, leading to the inequality: [ sum_{i=1}^{10} binom{m_i}{2} leq 2 binom{k}{2} ] where ( m_i ) is the number of subsets containing element ( i ).4. Simplifying the Inequality: - Convert the inequality to: [ sum_{i=1}^{10} m_i(m_i - 1) leq 2k(k - 1) ] - Using the Cauchy-Schwarz inequality, we find: [ sum_{i=1}^{10} m_i^2 geq frac{(5k)^2}{10} = frac{25k^2}{10} = frac{5k^2}{2} ] - Combining these results, we derive: [ frac{5k^2}{2} leq 2k^2 + 3k ] - Solving this inequality, we find ( k leq 6 ).5. Verification: - The derived upper bound ( k leq 6 ) is checked for feasibility by considering the design where each element appears in exactly 3 subsets, and each pair of subsets intersects in exactly 2 elements. This design satisfies all constraints and confirms the upper bound.Thus, the maximum value of ( k ) is (boxed{6}).]

Value of ( m ) such that the circle intersects the line ( x + 2y - 4 = 0 ) at points ( M ) and ( N ) with ( OM perp ON ): - Substitute ( x = 4 - 2y ) into the circle equation: [ 5y^2 - 16y + (8 + m) = 0 ] - Using Vieta's formulas, the product ( y_1y_2 = frac{8 + m}{5} ) and sum ( y_1 + y_2 = frac{16}{5} ). - For ( OM perp ON ), the condition ( x_1x_2 + y_1y_2 = 0 ) must hold: [ 16 - 8left(frac{16}{5}right) + 5left(frac{8 + m}{5}right) = 0 ] - Solving this gives ( m = frac{8}{5} ). - The value of ( m ) is (boxed{dfrac{8}{5}}).3. (K) is the midpoint of the arc (AD) not containing points (B) and (C). Given (angle O_1 K O_2 = 60^circ) and (K O_1 = 10), we need to find (O_1 O_2).Key steps:1. Cyclic Quadrilateral Properties: (ABCD) being cyclic implies that opposite angles sum to (180^circ). The midpoint (K) of arc (AD) is equidistant from (A) and (D) on the circumcircle.2. Conclusion: The symmetry and given angle imply (K O_1 = K O_2 = 10). Using the Law of Cosines in triangle (O_1 K O_2) confirms (O_1 O_2 = 10).[boxed{10}]]

🔑:Point K is the midpoint of arc AD, so BK is the bisector of the inscribed angle ABD, which means point O_{1} lies on segment BK. Similarly, point O_{2} lies on segment CK. The rays MO_{1} and MO_{2} are the bisectors of the vertical anglesAMB and CMD, so point M lies on segment O_{1}O_{2} and angle BMO_{1} = angle DMO_{2} = angle CMO_{2}.The inscribed angles ABD and ACD are equal. Therefore, angle MBO_{1} = angle MCO_{2}.By the exterior angle theorem of a triangle, angle KO_{1}O_{2} = angle MBO_{1} + angle BMO_{1} = angle MCO_{2} + angle CMO_{2} = angle KO_{2}O_{1}, so triangle O_{1}K_{2} is isosceles, and since one of its angles is 60^{circ}, this triangle is equilateral. Therefore, O_{1}O_{2} = KO_{1} = 10.## Answer10.
